### Sustainability and the environment {#Sustainability_and_the_environment}

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Floriade_Canberra_2010.jpg/220px-Floriade_Canberra_2010.jpg)](/wiki/File:Floriade_Canberra_2010.jpg) [Floriade](/wiki/Floriade_(Canberra) "Floriade (Canberra)") is held in [Commonwealth Park](/wiki/Commonwealth_Park "Commonwealth Park") every spring. It is the largest flower festival in the Southern Hemisphere, employing and encouraging environmental practises, including the use of [green energy](/wiki/Green_energy "Green energy").^[\[183\]](#cite_note-floriadeaustralia-183)^

The average Canberran was responsible for 13.7 tonnes of greenhouse gases in 2005.^[\[184\]](#cite_note-184)^ In 2012, the ACT Government legislated [greenhouse gas](/wiki/Greenhouse_gas "Greenhouse gas") targets to reduce its emissions by 40 per cent from 1990 levels by 2020, 80 per cent by 2050, with no net emissions by 2060.^[\[185\]](#cite_note-185)^ The government announced in 2013 a target for 90% of electricity consumed in the ACT to be supplied from renewable sources by 2020,^[\[186\]](#cite_note-renewable-186)^ and in 2016 set an ambitious target of 100% by 2020.^[\[187\]](#cite_note-187)^^[\[188\]](#cite_note-188)^{#cite_ref-188}

In 1996 Canberra became the first city in the world to set a vision of [no waste](/wiki/Zero_waste "Zero waste"), proposing an ambitious target of 2010 for completion.^[\[189\]](#cite_note-189)^ The strategy aimed to achieve a waste-free society by 2010, through the combined efforts of industry, government and community.^[\[190\]](#cite_note-190)^ By early 2010, it was apparent that though it had reduced waste going to landfill, the ACT initiative's original 2010 target for absolutely zero landfill waste would be delayed or revised to meet the reality.^[\[191\]](#cite_note-191)^^[\[192\]](#cite_note-192)^{#cite_ref-192}

[Plastic bags](/wiki/Plastic_bags "Plastic bags") made of [polyethylene](/wiki/Polyethylene "Polyethylene") polymer with a thickness of less than 35 [μm](/wiki/%CE%9Cm "Μm") were banned from retail distribution in the ACT from November 2011.^[\[193\]](#cite_note-193)^^[\[194\]](#cite_note-PlasticBags-194)^^[\[195\]](#cite_note-195)^ The ban was introduced by the ACT Government in an effort to make Canberra more sustainable.^[\[194\]](#cite_note-PlasticBags-194)^{#cite_ref-PlasticBags_194-1}

Of all waste produced in the ACT, 75 per cent is [recycled](/wiki/Recycled "Recycled").^[\[196\]](#cite_note-196)^ Average household [food waste](/wiki/Food_waste "Food waste") in the ACT remains above the Australian average, costing an average $641 per household per annum.^[\[197\]](#cite_note-197)^{#cite_ref-197}

Canberra's annual [Floriade](/wiki/Floriade_(Canberra) "Floriade (Canberra)") festival features a large display of flowers every Spring in [Commonwealth Park](/wiki/Commonwealth_Park "Commonwealth Park"). The organisers of the event have a strong environmental standpoint, promoting and using [green energy](/wiki/Green_energy "Green energy"), "green catering", [sustainable paper](/wiki/Sustainability "Sustainability"), the conservation and saving of water.^[\[183\]](#cite_note-floriadeaustralia-183)^ The event is also smoke-free.^[\[183\]](#cite_note-floriadeaustralia-183)^{#cite_ref-floriadeaustralia_183-2}  

Government and politics {#Government_and_politics}
--------------------------------------------------

### Territory government {#Territory_government}

See also: [Australian Capital Territory Legislative Assembly](/wiki/Australian_Capital_Territory_Legislative_Assembly "Australian Capital Territory Legislative Assembly") and [Electoral systems of the Australian states and territories](/wiki/Electoral_systems_of_the_Australian_states_and_territories "Electoral systems of the Australian states and territories")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Entrance_to_the_ACT_Legislative_Assembly_building_July_2022.jpg/220px-Entrance_to_the_ACT_Legislative_Assembly_building_July_2022.jpg)](/wiki/File:Entrance_to_the_ACT_Legislative_Assembly_building_July_2022.jpg) ACT Legislative Assembly   
and the statue *Ethos* (Tom Bass, 1961)

There is no local council or city government for the city of Canberra. The [Australian Capital Territory Legislative Assembly](/wiki/Australian_Capital_Territory_Legislative_Assembly "Australian Capital Territory Legislative Assembly") performs the roles of both a [city council](/wiki/City_council "City council") for the city and a territory government for the rest of the Australian Capital Territory.^[\[124\]](#cite_note-ass-124)^ However, the vast majority of the population of the Territory reside in Canberra and the city is therefore the primary focus of the ACT Government.{#cite_ref-ass_124-2}

The assembly consists of 25 members elected from five districts using proportional representation. The five districts are [Brindabella](/wiki/Brindabella_electorate "Brindabella electorate"), [Ginninderra](/wiki/Ginninderra_electorate "Ginninderra electorate"), [Kurrajong](/wiki/Kurrajong_electorate "Kurrajong electorate"), [Murrumbidgee](/wiki/Murrumbidgee_electorate "Murrumbidgee electorate") and [Yerrabi](/wiki/Yerrabi_electorate "Yerrabi electorate"), which each elect five members.^[\[198\]](#cite_note-elecpage-198)^ The Chief Minister is elected by the Members of the Legislative Assembly (MLA) and selects colleagues to serve as ministers alongside him or her in the Executive, known informally as the cabinet.^[\[124\]](#cite_note-ass-124)^{#cite_ref-ass_124-3}

Whereas the ACT has federally been dominated by Labor,^[\[199\]](#cite_note-ABCelections2007-199)^^[\[200\]](#cite_note-fras-200)^ the Liberals have been able to gain some footing in the ACT Legislative Assembly and were in government during a period of
6+1⁄2 years from 1995 and 2001. Labor took back control of the Assembly in 2001.^[\[125\]](#cite_note-state_el-125)^ At the 2004 election, Chief Minister [Jon Stanhope](/wiki/Jon_Stanhope "Jon Stanhope") and the Labor Party won 9 of the 17 seats allowing them to form the ACT's first majority government.^[\[125\]](#cite_note-state_el-125)^ Since 2008, the ACT has been governed by a coalition of Labor and the Greens.^[\[125\]](#cite_note-state_el-125)^^[\[201\]](#cite_note-anniv-201)^^[\[202\]](#cite_note-202)^ As of 2022^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Canberra&action=edit)^, the Chief Minister was [Andrew Barr](/wiki/Andrew_Barr "Andrew Barr") from the Australian Labor Party.{#cite_ref-202}

The Australian federal government retains some influence over the ACT government. In the administrative sphere, most frequently this is through the actions of the [National Capital Authority](/wiki/National_Capital_Authority "National Capital Authority") which is responsible for planning and development in areas of Canberra which are considered to be of national importance or which are central to Griffin's plan for the city,^[\[203\]](#cite_note-nca-203)^ such as the Parliamentary Triangle, Lake Burley Griffin, major approach and processional roads, areas where the Commonwealth retains ownership of the land or undeveloped hills and ridge-lines (which form part of the Canberra Nature Park).^[\[203\]](#cite_note-nca-203)^^[\[204\]](#cite_note-204)^^[\[205\]](#cite_note-205)^ The national government also retains a level of control over the Territory Assembly through the provisions of the *[Australian Capital Territory (Self-Government) Act 1988](/wiki/Australian_Capital_Territory_(Self-Government)_Act_1988 "Australian Capital Territory (Self-Government) Act 1988")* .^[\[206\]](#cite_note-206)^ This federal act defines the legislative power of the ACT assembly.^[\[207\]](#cite_note-207)^{#cite_ref-207}  

### Federal representation {#Federal_representation}

The ACT was given its first federal parliamentary representation in 1949 when it gained a seat in the House of Representatives, the [Division of Australian Capital Territory](/wiki/Division_of_Australian_Capital_Territory "Division of Australian Capital Territory").^[\[208\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTESparke1988289-208)^^[\[209\]](#cite_note-1948act-209)^ However, until 1966, the ACT member could only vote on matters directly affecting the territory and did not count for purposes of forming government.^[\[209\]](#cite_note-1948act-209)^ In 1974, the ACT was allocated two Senate seats and the House of Representatives seat was divided into two.^[\[208\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTESparke1988289-208)^ A third was created in 1996, but was abolished in 1998 because of changes to the regional demographic distribution.^[\[199\]](#cite_note-ABCelections2007-199)^ At the 2019 election, the third seat has been reintroduced as the [Division of Bean](/wiki/Division_of_Bean "Division of Bean").{#cite_ref-ABCelections2007_199-1}

The House of Representatives seats have mostly been held by Labor and usually by comfortable margins.^[\[199\]](#cite_note-ABCelections2007-199)^^[\[200\]](#cite_note-fras-200)^ The Labor Party has polled at least seven percentage points more than the [Liberal Party](/wiki/Liberal_Party_of_Australia "Liberal Party of Australia") at every federal election since 1990 and their average lead since then has been 15 percentage points.^[\[125\]](#cite_note-state_el-125)^ The ALP and the Liberal Party held one Senate seat each until the [2022 election](/wiki/2022_Australian_federal_election "2022 Australian federal election") when Independent candidate [David Pocock](/wiki/David_Pocock "David Pocock") unseated the Liberal candidate [Zed Seselja](/wiki/Zed_Seselja "Zed Seselja").^[\[210\]](#cite_note-210)^{#cite_ref-210}  

### Judiciary and policing {#Judiciary_and_policing}

Main articles: [Magistrates Court of the Australian Capital Territory](/wiki/Magistrates_Court_of_the_Australian_Capital_Territory "Magistrates Court of the Australian Capital Territory"), [Supreme Court of the Australian Capital Territory](/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_Australian_Capital_Territory "Supreme Court of the Australian Capital Territory"), and [ACT Policing](/wiki/ACT_Policing "ACT Policing")  
See also: [Crime in the Australian Capital Territory](/wiki/Crime_in_the_Australian_Capital_Territory "Crime in the Australian Capital Territory")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/High_Court_of_Australia_building%2C_Canberra_03.jpg/220px-High_Court_of_Australia_building%2C_Canberra_03.jpg)](/wiki/File:High_Court_of_Australia_building,_Canberra_03.jpg) [High Court of Australia](/wiki/High_Court_of_Australia "High Court of Australia")

The [Australian Federal Police](/wiki/Australian_Federal_Police "Australian Federal Police") (AFP) provides all of the constabulary services in the territory in a manner similar to state police forces, under a contractual agreement with the ACT Government.^[\[211\]](#cite_note-211)^ The AFP does so through its community policing arm [ACT Policing](/wiki/ACT_Policing "ACT Policing").^[\[212\]](#cite_note-afpact-212)^{#cite_ref-afpact_212-0}

People who have been charged with offences are tried either in the [ACT Magistrates Court](/wiki/Magistrates_Court_of_the_Australian_Capital_Territory "Magistrates Court of the Australian Capital Territory") or, for more severe offences, the [ACT Supreme Court](/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_Australian_Capital_Territory "Supreme Court of the Australian Capital Territory").^[\[213\]](#cite_note-213)^ Prior to its closure in 2009, prisoners were held in [remand](/wiki/Remand_(detention) "Remand (detention)") at the [Belconnen Remand Centre](/wiki/Belconnen_Remand_Centre "Belconnen Remand Centre") in the ACT but usually imprisoned in New South Wales.^[\[214\]](#cite_note-214)^ The [Alexander Maconochie Centre](/wiki/Alexander_Maconochie_Centre "Alexander Maconochie Centre") was officially opened on 11 September 2008 by then Chief Minister [Jon Stanhope](/wiki/Jon_Stanhope "Jon Stanhope"). The total cost for construction was $130 million.^[\[215\]](#cite_note-215)^ The [ACT Civil and Administrative Tribunal](/wiki/ACT_Civil_and_Administrative_Tribunal "ACT Civil and Administrative Tribunal") deal with minor civil law actions and other various legal matters.^[\[216\]](#cite_note-216)^^[\[217\]](#cite_note-217)^{#cite_ref-217}

Canberra has the lowest rate of crime of any capital city in [Australia](/wiki/Australia "Australia") as of 2019^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Canberra&action=edit)^.^[\[218\]](#cite_note-218)^ As of 2016^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Canberra&action=edit)^ the most common crimes in the ACT were property related crimes, unlawful entry with intent and [motor vehicle theft](/wiki/Motor_vehicle_theft "Motor vehicle theft"). They affected 2,304 and 966 people (580 and 243 per 100,000 persons respectively). [Homicide](/wiki/Homicide "Homicide") and related offences---murder, attempted murder and manslaughter, but excluding driving causing death and conspiracy to murder---affect 1.0 per 100,000 persons, which is below the national average of 1.9 per 100,000. Rates of [sexual assault](/wiki/Sexual_assault "Sexual assault") (64.4 per 100,000 persons) are also below the national average (98.5 per 100,000).^[\[219\]](#cite_note-219)^^[\[220\]](#cite_note-220)^^[\[221\]](#cite_note-221)^ However the 2017 crime statistics showed a rise in some types of personal crime, notably burglaries, thefts and assaults.{#cite_ref-221}  

Economy {#Economy}
------------------

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/220_London_Circuit_May_2021.jpg/220px-220_London_Circuit_May_2021.jpg)](/wiki/File:220_London_Circuit_May_2021.jpg) Just under a third of Canberrans are employed in the public sector, working in government departments such as the [ACT Government](/wiki/Government_of_the_Australian_Capital_Territory "Government of the Australian Capital Territory")

In February 2020, the unemployment rate in Canberra was 2.9% which was lower than the national unemployment rate of 5.1%.^[\[222\]](#cite_note-222)^ As a result of low unemployment and substantial levels of public sector and commercial employment, Canberra has the highest average level of [disposable income](/wiki/Disposable_income "Disposable income") of any Australian capital city.^[\[223\]](#cite_note-223)^ The gross average weekly wage in Canberra is [$](/wiki/Australian_dollar "Australian dollar")1827 compared with the national average of $1658 (November 2019).^[\[224\]](#cite_note-CMTED_Brief-224)^{#cite_ref-CMTED_Brief_224-0}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/50_Marcus_Clarke_Street_Feb_2016.jpg/220px-50_Marcus_Clarke_Street_Feb_2016.jpg)](/wiki/File:50_Marcus_Clarke_Street_Feb_2016.jpg) The [Civic](/wiki/Civic,_Australian_Capital_Territory "Civic, Australian Capital Territory") is home to various administrative departments, such as the [Department of Education, Skills and Employment](/wiki/Department_of_Education,_Skills_and_Employment "Department of Education, Skills and Employment")

The median house price in Canberra as of February 2020 was $745,000, lower than only Sydney among capital cities of more than 100,000 people, having surpassed Melbourne and Perth since 2005.^[\[224\]](#cite_note-CMTED_Brief-224)^^[\[225\]](#cite_note-225)^^[\[226\]](#cite_note-226)^ The median weekly rent paid by Canberra residents is higher than rents in all other states and territories.^[\[227\]](#cite_note-227)^ As of January 2014 the median unit rent in Canberra was $410 per week and median housing rent was $460, making the city the third most expensive in the country.^[\[228\]](#cite_note-228)^ Factors contributing to this higher weekly rental market include; higher average weekly incomes, restricted land supply,^[\[229\]](#cite_note-229)^ and inflationary clauses in the ACT Residential Tenancies Act.^[\[230\]](#cite_note-230)^{#cite_ref-230}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Bunda_Street_July_2021.jpg/220px-Bunda_Street_July_2021.jpg)](/wiki/File:Bunda_Street_July_2021.jpg) [Bunda Street](/wiki/Bunda_Street "Bunda Street") in Canberra's shopping district; tourism, retail and hospitality are also major employers.

The city's main industry is public administration and safety, which accounted for 27.1% of Gross Territory Product in 2018-19 and employed 32.49% of Canberra's workforce.^[\[231\]](#cite_note-231)^^[\[21\]](#cite_note-EDA_ACT_Economic_Indicators-21)^ The headquarters of many [Australian Public Service](/wiki/Australian_Public_Service "Australian Public Service") agencies are located in Canberra, and Canberra is also host to several [Australian Defence Force](/wiki/Australian_Defence_Force "Australian Defence Force") establishments, most notably the Australian Defence Force headquarters and [HMAS *Harman*](/wiki/HMAS_Harman "HMAS Harman"), which is a naval communications centre that is being converted into a tri-service, multi-user depot.^[\[232\]](#cite_note-232)^ Other major sectors by employment include Health Care (10.54%), Professional Services (9.77%), Education and Training (9.64%), Retail (7.27%), Accommodation \& Food (6.39%) and Construction (5.80%).{#cite_ref-232}

^[\[21\]](#cite_note-EDA_ACT_Economic_Indicators-21)^{#cite_ref-EDA_ACT_Economic_Indicators_21-2}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/NASA%27s_Deep_Space_Antenna_Upgrade_to_Affect_Voyager.jpg/220px-NASA%27s_Deep_Space_Antenna_Upgrade_to_Affect_Voyager.jpg)](/wiki/File:NASA%27s_Deep_Space_Antenna_Upgrade_to_Affect_Voyager.jpg) A growing number of Canberrans work in the science and technology sector, such as at the [Canberra Deep Space Communication Complex](/wiki/Canberra_Deep_Space_Communication_Complex "Canberra Deep Space Communication Complex").

The former [RAAF Fairbairn](/wiki/Fairbairn_Airbase "Fairbairn Airbase"), adjacent to the [Canberra Airport](/wiki/Canberra_Airport "Canberra Airport") was sold to the operators of the airport,^[\[233\]](#cite_note-fb-233)^ but the base continues to be used for [RAAF](/wiki/RAAF "RAAF") VIP flights.^[\[234\]](#cite_note-234)^^[\[235\]](#cite_note-235)^ A growing number of software vendors have based themselves in Canberra, to capitalise on the concentration of government customers; these include [Tower Software](/wiki/Tower_Software "Tower Software") and [RuleBurst](/wiki/RuleBurst "RuleBurst").^[\[236\]](#cite_note-236)^^[\[237\]](#cite_note-237)^ A consortium of private and government investors is making plans for a billion-dollar data hub, with the aim of making Canberra a leading centre of such activity in the Asia-Pacific region.^[\[238\]](#cite_note-238)^ A Canberra Cyber Security Innovation Node was established in 2019 to grow the ACT's cyber security sector and related space, defence and education industries.^[\[239\]](#cite_note-239)^{#cite_ref-239}  

Demographics {#Demographics}
----------------------------

Main article: [Demographics of Canberra](/wiki/Demographics_of_Canberra "Demographics of Canberra")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Belconnen_Apartments_-_DSC07473-HDR.jpg/220px-Belconnen_Apartments_-_DSC07473-HDR.jpg)](/wiki/File:Belconnen_Apartments_-_DSC07473-HDR.jpg) High-density residential apartments in [Belconnen](/wiki/Belconnen "Belconnen"); Canberra has one of the fastest growing populations in the nation^[\[240\]](#cite_note-:6-240)^

At the [2021 census](/wiki/2021_Australian_census "2021 Australian census"), the population of Canberra was 453,558,^[\[240\]](#cite_note-:6-240)^ up from 395,790 at the 2016 census,^[\[241\]](#cite_note-Census2016-241)^ and 355,596 at the [2011 census](/wiki/2011_Australian_census "2011 Australian census").^[\[242\]](#cite_note-Census2011-242)^ Canberra has been the fastest-growing city in Australia in recent years, having grown 23.3% from 2011 to 2021.^[\[240\]](#cite_note-:6-240)^{#cite_ref-:6_240-2}

Canberrans are relatively young, highly [mobile](/wiki/Population_mobility "Population mobility") and well educated. The median age is 35 years and only 12.7% of the population is aged over 65 years.^[\[241\]](#cite_note-Census2016-241)^ Between 1996 and 2001, 61.9% of the population either moved to or from Canberra, which was the second highest mobility rate of any Australian capital city.^[\[243\]](#cite_note-243)^ As at May 2017, 43% of ACT residents (25--64) had a level of educational attainment equal to at least a [bachelor's degree](/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree "Bachelor's degree"), significantly higher that the national average of 31%.^[\[244\]](#cite_note-244)^{#cite_ref-244}

According to statistics collected by the [National Australia Bank](/wiki/National_Australia_Bank "National Australia Bank") and reported in *The Canberra Times* , Canberrans on average give significantly more money to charity than Australians in other states and territories, for both dollar giving and as a proportion of income.^[\[245\]](#cite_note-245)^{#cite_ref-245}  

### Ancestry and immigration {#Ancestry_and_immigration}

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Canberra_Candle_Festival_2016_%28203914161%29.jpeg/220px-Canberra_Candle_Festival_2016_%28203914161%29.jpeg)](/wiki/File:Canberra_Candle_Festival_2016_(203914161).jpeg) The annual Canberra Nara Candle Festival {#cite_ref-246}

|          Birthplace^[\[N 1\]](#cite_note-246)^          | Population |
|---------------------------------------------------------|------------|
| [Australia](/wiki/Australia "Australia")                | 269,682    |
| [England](/wiki/England "England")                      | 12,739     |
| [Mainland China](/wiki/Mainland_China "Mainland China") | 11,334     |
| [India](/wiki/India "India")                            | 10,405     |
| [New Zealand](/wiki/New_Zealand "New Zealand")          | 4,722      |
| [Philippines](/wiki/Philippines "Philippines")          | 3,789      |
| [Vietnam](/wiki/Vietnam "Vietnam")                      | 3,340      |
| [United States](/wiki/United_States "United States")    | 2,775      |
| [Sri Lanka](/wiki/Sri_Lanka "Sri Lanka")                | 2,774      |
| [Malaysia](/wiki/Malaysia "Malaysia")                   | 2,431      |
| [South Korea](/wiki/South_Korea "South Korea")          | 2,283      |
[Country of birth (2016)^[\[22\]](#cite_note-quickstats.censusdata.abs.gov.au-22)^]

{#cite_ref-quickstats.censusdata.abs.gov.au_22-1}

At the 2016 census, the most commonly nominated ancestries were:^[\[N 2\]](#cite_note-247)^^[\[22\]](#cite_note-quickstats.censusdata.abs.gov.au-22)^{#cite_ref-quickstats.censusdata.abs.gov.au_22-2}  
* [English](/wiki/English_Australians "English Australians") (35%)
* [Australian](/wiki/Australians "Australians") (34%)^[\[N 3\]](#cite_note-249)^{#cite_ref-249}
* [Irish](/wiki/Irish_Australians "Irish Australians") (14%)
* [Scottish](/wiki/Scottish_Australians "Scottish Australians") (11%)
* [Chinese](/wiki/Chinese_Australians "Chinese Australians") (6%)
* [German](/wiki/German_Australians "German Australians") (4.7%)
* [Indian](/wiki/Indian_Australians "Indian Australians") (3.9%)
* [Italian](/wiki/Italian_Australians "Italian Australians") (3.5%)
* [Dutch](/wiki/Dutch_Australians "Dutch Australians") (1.7%)
* [Indigenous](/wiki/Indigenous_Australians "Indigenous Australians") (1.6%)^[\[N 4\]](#cite_note-250)^{#cite_ref-250}
* [Filipino](/wiki/Filipino_Australians "Filipino Australians") (1.3%)
* [Vietnamese](/wiki/Vietnamese_Australians "Vietnamese Australians") (1.3%)
* [Greek](/wiki/Greek_Australians "Greek Australians") (1.3%)
* [Croatian](/wiki/Croatian_Australians "Croatian Australians") (1.2%)
* [Polish](/wiki/Polish_Australians "Polish Australians") (1.1%)

The 2016 census showed that 32% of Canberra's inhabitants were [born overseas](/wiki/Immigration_to_Australia "Immigration to Australia").^[\[22\]](#cite_note-quickstats.censusdata.abs.gov.au-22)^ Of inhabitants born outside Australia, the most prevalent countries of birth were England, China, India, New Zealand and the Philippines.^[\[247\]](#cite_note-251)^{#cite_ref-251}

1.6% of the population, or 6,476 people, identified as [Indigenous Australians](/wiki/Indigenous_Australians "Indigenous Australians") ([Aboriginal Australians](/wiki/Aboriginal_Australians "Aboriginal Australians") and [Torres Strait Islanders](/wiki/Torres_Strait_Islanders "Torres Strait Islanders")) in 2016.^[\[N 5\]](#cite_note-252)^^[\[22\]](#cite_note-quickstats.censusdata.abs.gov.au-22)^{#cite_ref-quickstats.censusdata.abs.gov.au_22-4}  

### Language {#Language}

At the 2016 census, 72.7% of people spoke only English at home. The other languages most commonly spoken at home were [Mandarin](/wiki/Standard_Mandarin "Standard Mandarin") (3.1%), [Vietnamese](/wiki/Vietnamese_language "Vietnamese language") (1.1%), [Cantonese](/wiki/Cantonese "Cantonese") (1%), [Hindi](/wiki/Hindi "Hindi") (0.9%) and [Spanish](/wiki/Spanish_language "Spanish language") (0.8%).^[\[22\]](#cite_note-quickstats.censusdata.abs.gov.au-22)^{#cite_ref-quickstats.censusdata.abs.gov.au_22-5}  

### Religion {#Religion}

On census night in 2016, approximately 50.0% of ACT residents described themselves as Christian (excluding not stated responses), the most common denominations being [Catholic](/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_Australia "Catholic Church in Australia") and [Anglican](/wiki/Anglican_Church_of_Australia "Anglican Church of Australia"); 36.2% described themselves as having no religion.^[\[241\]](#cite_note-Census2016-241)^{#cite_ref-Census2016_241-2}  

Culture {#Culture}
------------------

### Education {#Education}

Main article: [Education in the Australian Capital Territory](/wiki/Education_in_the_Australian_Capital_Territory "Education in the Australian Capital Territory")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/ANU_School_of_Art%2C_Canberra.jpg/220px-ANU_School_of_Art%2C_Canberra.jpg)](/wiki/File:ANU_School_of_Art,_Canberra.jpg) [ANU](/wiki/Australian_National_University "Australian National University") School of Art (formerly the Canberra High School)

The two main tertiary institutions are the [Australian National University](/wiki/Australian_National_University "Australian National University") (ANU) in [Acton](/wiki/Acton,_Australian_Capital_Territory "Acton, Australian Capital Territory") and the [University of Canberra](/wiki/University_of_Canberra "University of Canberra") (UC) in [Bruce](/wiki/Bruce,_Australian_Capital_Territory "Bruce, Australian Capital Territory"), with over 10,500 and 8,000 full-time-equivalent students respectively.^[\[248\]](#cite_note-253)^^[\[249\]](#cite_note-anu-254)^ Established in 1946,^[\[250\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGibbney1988258–262-255)^ the ANU has always had a strong research focus and is ranked among the leading universities in the world and the best in Australia by *[The Times Higher Education Supplement](/wiki/The_Times_Higher_Education_Supplement "The Times Higher Education Supplement")* and the Shanghai Jiao Tong World University Rankings.^[\[249\]](#cite_note-anu-254)^^[\[251\]](#cite_note-256)^ There are two religious university campuses in Canberra: Signadou in the northern suburb of [Watson](/wiki/Watson,_Australian_Capital_Territory "Watson, Australian Capital Territory") is a campus of the [Australian Catholic University](/wiki/Australian_Catholic_University "Australian Catholic University");^[\[252\]](#cite_note-257)^ St Mark's Theological College in [Barton](/wiki/Barton,_Australian_Capital_Territory "Barton, Australian Capital Territory") is part of the secular [Charles Sturt University](/wiki/Charles_Sturt_University "Charles Sturt University").^[\[253\]](#cite_note-258)^ The ACT Government announced on 5 March 2020 that the CIT campus and an adjoining carpark in [Reid](/wiki/Reid,_Australian_Capital_Territory "Reid, Australian Capital Territory") would be leased to the [University of New South Wales](/wiki/University_of_New_South_Wales "University of New South Wales") (UNSW) for a [peppercorn lease](/wiki/Peppercorn_lease "Peppercorn lease"), for it to develop as a campus for a new UNSW Canberra.^[\[254\]](#cite_note-2020-03-05_ABC-259)^ UNSW released a master plan in 2021 for a 6,000 student campus to be realised over 15 years at a cost of $1 billion.^[\[255\]](#cite_note-260)^{#cite_ref-260}

The [Australian Defence College](/wiki/Australian_Defence_College "Australian Defence College") has two campuses: the Australian Command and Staff College (ACSC) plus the Centre for Defence and Strategic Studies (CDSS) at [Weston](/wiki/Weston,_Australian_Capital_Territory "Weston, Australian Capital Territory"), and the [Australian Defence Force Academy](/wiki/Australian_Defence_Force_Academy "Australian Defence Force Academy") (ADFA) beside the [Royal Military College, Duntroon](/wiki/Royal_Military_College,_Duntroon "Royal Military College, Duntroon") located in the inner-northern suburb of [Campbell](/wiki/Campbell,_Australian_Capital_Territory "Campbell, Australian Capital Territory").^[\[256\]](#cite_note-261)^^[\[257\]](#cite_note-262)^ ADFA teaches military undergraduates and [postgraduates](/wiki/Quaternary_education "Quaternary education") and includes UNSW@ADFA, a campus of the [University of New South Wales](/wiki/University_of_New_South_Wales "University of New South Wales");^[\[258\]](#cite_note-263)^^[\[259\]](#cite_note-264)^ Duntroon provides [Australian Army](/wiki/Australian_Army "Australian Army") [officer](/wiki/Officer_(armed_forces) "Officer (armed forces)") training.^[\[260\]](#cite_note-265)^{#cite_ref-265}

Tertiary level vocational education is also available through the [Canberra Institute of Technology](/wiki/Canberra_Institute_of_Technology "Canberra Institute of Technology") (CIT), with campuses in [Bruce](/wiki/Bruce,_Australian_Capital_Territory "Bruce, Australian Capital Territory"), Reid, [Gungahlin](/wiki/Gungahlin "Gungahlin"), [Tuggeranong](/wiki/Tuggeranong "Tuggeranong") and [Fyshwick](/wiki/Fyshwick "Fyshwick").^[\[261\]](#cite_note-266)^ The combined enrolment of the CIT campuses was over 28,000 students in 2019.^[\[262\]](#cite_note-267)^ Following the transfer of land in Reid for the new UNSW Canberra, a new CIT [Woden](/wiki/Woden_Valley "Woden Valley") is scheduled to be completed by 2025.^[\[263\]](#cite_note-268)^{#cite_ref-268}

In 2016 there were 132 [schools](/wiki/List_of_schools_in_the_Australian_Capital_Territory "List of schools in the Australian Capital Territory") in Canberra; 87 were operated by the government and 45 were private.^[\[264\]](#cite_note-269)^ During 2006, the ACT Government announced closures of up to 39 schools, to take effect from the end of the school year, and after a series of consultations unveiled its *Towards 2020: Renewing Our Schools* policy.^[\[265\]](#cite_note-270)^ As a result, some schools closed during the 2006--08 period, while others were merged; the creation of combined primary and secondary government schools was to proceed over a decade. The closure of schools provoked significant opposition.^[\[266\]](#cite_note-271)^^[\[267\]](#cite_note-272)^^[\[268\]](#cite_note-273)^ Most suburbs were planned to include a primary and a nearby preschool; these were usually located near open areas where recreational and sporting activities were easily available.^[\[269\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUniversal_Publishers20071–90-274)^ Canberra also has the highest percentage of non-government (private) school students in Australia, accounting for 40.6 per cent of ACT enrollments.^[\[270\]](#cite_note-275)^{#cite_ref-275}  

### Arts and entertainment {#Arts_and_entertainment}

See also: [Music of Canberra](/wiki/Music_of_Canberra "Music of Canberra")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/National_Film_and_Sound_Archive%2C_Canberra%2C_2022%2C_03_%282%29.jpg/220px-National_Film_and_Sound_Archive%2C_Canberra%2C_2022%2C_03_%282%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:National_Film_and_Sound_Archive,_Canberra,_2022,_03_(2).jpg) [National Film and Sound Archive](/wiki/National_Film_and_Sound_Archive "National Film and Sound Archive")

Canberra is home to many national monuments and institutions such as the [Australian War Memorial](/wiki/Australian_War_Memorial "Australian War Memorial"), the [Australian Institute of Aboriginal and Torres Strait Islander Studies](/wiki/Australian_Institute_of_Aboriginal_and_Torres_Strait_Islander_Studies "Australian Institute of Aboriginal and Torres Strait Islander Studies"), the [National Gallery of Australia](/wiki/National_Gallery_of_Australia "National Gallery of Australia"), the [National Portrait Gallery](/wiki/National_Portrait_Gallery_(Australia) "National Portrait Gallery (Australia)"), the [National Library](/wiki/National_Library_of_Australia "National Library of Australia"),^[\[174\]](#cite_note-map-174)^ the [National Archives](/wiki/National_Archives_of_Australia "National Archives of Australia"),^[\[271\]](#cite_note-276)^ the [Australian Academy of Science](/wiki/Australian_Academy_of_Science "Australian Academy of Science"),^[\[272\]](#cite_note-277)^ the [National Film \& Sound Archive](/wiki/National_Film_%26_Sound_Archive "National Film & Sound Archive") and the [National Museum](/wiki/National_Museum_of_Australia "National Museum of Australia").^[\[174\]](#cite_note-map-174)^ Many Commonwealth government buildings in Canberra are open to the public, including [Parliament House](/wiki/Parliament_House,_Canberra "Parliament House, Canberra"), the [High Court](/wiki/High_Court_of_Australia "High Court of Australia") and the [Royal Australian Mint](/wiki/Royal_Australian_Mint "Royal Australian Mint").^[\[273\]](#cite_note-278)^^[\[274\]](#cite_note-279)^^[\[275\]](#cite_note-280)^{#cite_ref-280}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/National_Museum_of_Australia_03.jpg/220px-National_Museum_of_Australia_03.jpg)](/wiki/File:National_Museum_of_Australia_03.jpg) The [National Museum of Australia](/wiki/National_Museum_of_Australia "National Museum of Australia") established in 2001 records Australia's social history and is one of Canberra's more architecturally daring buildings.

Lake Burley Griffin is the site of the [Captain James Cook Memorial](/wiki/Captain_James_Cook_Memorial "Captain James Cook Memorial") and the [National Carillon](/wiki/National_Carillon "National Carillon").^[\[174\]](#cite_note-map-174)^ Other sites of interest include the [Australian--American Memorial](/wiki/Australian%E2%80%93American_Memorial "Australian–American Memorial"), [Commonwealth Park](/wiki/Commonwealth_Park "Commonwealth Park"), [Commonwealth Place](/wiki/Commonwealth_Place,_Canberra "Commonwealth Place, Canberra"), the [Telstra Tower](/wiki/Telstra_Tower "Telstra Tower"), the [Australian National Botanic Gardens](/wiki/Australian_National_Botanic_Gardens "Australian National Botanic Gardens"), the [National Zoo and Aquarium](/wiki/National_Zoo_and_Aquarium "National Zoo and Aquarium"), the [National Dinosaur Museum](/wiki/National_Dinosaur_Museum "National Dinosaur Museum"), and [Questacon -- the National Science and Technology Centre](/wiki/National_Science_and_Technology_Centre,_Canberra "National Science and Technology Centre, Canberra").^[\[174\]](#cite_note-map-174)^^[\[276\]](#cite_note-281)^{#cite_ref-281}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/War_memorial_01.jpg/220px-War_memorial_01.jpg)](/wiki/File:War_memorial_01.jpg) The [Australian War Memorial](/wiki/Australian_War_Memorial "Australian War Memorial")

The [Canberra Museum and Gallery](/wiki/Canberra_Museum_and_Gallery "Canberra Museum and Gallery") in [the city](/wiki/Civic,_Australian_Capital_Territory "Civic, Australian Capital Territory") is a repository of local history and art, housing a permanent collection and visiting exhibitions.^[\[277\]](#cite_note-282)^ Several historic homes are open to the public: Lanyon and Tuggeranong Homesteads in the [Tuggeranong Valley](/wiki/Tuggeranong "Tuggeranong"),^[\[278\]](#cite_note-283)^^[\[279\]](#cite_note-284)^ Mugga-Mugga in [Symonston](/wiki/Symonston,_Australian_Capital_Territory "Symonston, Australian Capital Territory"),^[\[280\]](#cite_note-285)^ and Blundells' Cottage in [Parkes](/wiki/Parkes,_Australian_Capital_Territory "Parkes, Australian Capital Territory") all display the lifestyle of the early European settlers.^[\[39\]](#cite_note-BLUNDELL-39)^ [Calthorpes' House](/wiki/Calthorpes%27_House "Calthorpes' House") in [Red Hill](/wiki/Red_Hill,_Australian_Capital_Territory "Red Hill, Australian Capital Territory") is a well-preserved example of a 1920s house from Canberra's very early days.^[\[281\]](#cite_note-286)^ [Strathnairn Homestead](/wiki/Strathnairn_Homestead,_Australian_Capital_Territory "Strathnairn Homestead, Australian Capital Territory") is an historic building which also dates from the 1920s.{#cite_ref-286}

Canberra has many venues for live music and theatre: the [Canberra Theatre and Playhouse](/wiki/Canberra_Theatre "Canberra Theatre") which hosts many major concerts and productions;^[\[282\]](#cite_note-287)^ and Llewellyn Hall (within the [ANU School of Music](/wiki/ANU_School_of_Music "ANU School of Music")), a world-class concert hall are two of the most notable.^[\[283\]](#cite_note-rg-288)^ The Street Theatre is a venue with less mainstream offerings.^[\[283\]](#cite_note-rg-288)^ [The Albert Hall](/wiki/Albert_Hall,_Canberra "Albert Hall, Canberra") was the city's first performing arts venue, opened in 1928. It was the original performance venue for theatre groups such as the Canberra Repertory Society.^[\[284\]](#cite_note-289)^{#cite_ref-289}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Canberra_Skyfire_2017_%28203911129%29.jpeg/220px-Canberra_Skyfire_2017_%28203911129%29.jpeg)](/wiki/File:Canberra_Skyfire_2017_(203911129).jpeg) The annual Skyfire fireworks display over Lake Burley Griffin, held during the [Enlighten Festival](/wiki/Enlighten_Canberra "Enlighten Canberra")

[Stonefest](/wiki/Stonefest "Stonefest") was a large annual festival, for some years one of the biggest festivals in Canberra.^[\[285\]](#cite_note-290)^^[\[286\]](#cite_note-291)^ It was downsized and rebranded as Stone Day in 2012.^[\[287\]](#cite_note-292)^ There are numerous bars and nightclubs which also offer live entertainment, particularly concentrated in the areas of [Dickson](/wiki/Dickson,_Australian_Capital_Territory "Dickson, Australian Capital Territory"), [Kingston](/wiki/Kingston,_Australian_Capital_Territory "Kingston, Australian Capital Territory") and [the city](/wiki/City,_Australian_Capital_Territory "City, Australian Capital Territory").^[\[288\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVaisutis2009283–285-293)^ Most town centres have facilities for a community theatre and a cinema, and they all have a library.^[\[289\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUniversal_Publishers200710–12-294)^ Popular cultural events include the [National Folk Festival](/wiki/National_Folk_Festival_(Australia) "National Folk Festival (Australia)"), the [Royal Canberra Show](/wiki/Royal_Canberra_Show "Royal Canberra Show"), the [Summernats](/wiki/Summernats "Summernats") car festival, [Enlighten](/wiki/Enlighten_Canberra "Enlighten Canberra") festival, the [National Multicultural Festival](/wiki/National_Multicultural_Festival "National Multicultural Festival") in February and the *Celebrate Canberra* festival held over 10 days in March in conjunction with Canberra Day.^[\[290\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVaisutis2009278-295)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVaisutis2009278_295-0}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Toku_in_the_Nara_Peace_Park_June_2014.jpg/220px-Toku_in_the_Nara_Peace_Park_June_2014.jpg)](/wiki/File:Toku_in_the_Nara_Peace_Park_June_2014.jpg) *Toku* in the Canberra-Nara Peace Park, which is located in the [Lennox Gardens](/wiki/Lennox_Gardens "Lennox Gardens")

Canberra maintains sister-city relationships with both [Nara](/wiki/Nara,_Nara "Nara, Nara"), Japan and Beijing, China. Canberra has friendship-city relationships with both [Dili](/wiki/Dili "Dili"), East Timor and [Hangzhou](/wiki/Hangzhou "Hangzhou"), China.^[\[291\]](#cite_note-Canberra-296)^ City-to-city relationships encourage communities and special interest groups both locally and abroad to engage in a wide range of exchange activities. The Canberra Nara Candle Festival held annually in spring, is a community celebration of the Canberra Nara Sister City relationship.^[\[292\]](#cite_note-297)^ The festival is held in Canberra Nara Park on the shores of Lake Burley Griffin.^[\[293\]](#cite_note-298)^{#cite_ref-298}

The history of Canberra was told in the 1938 radio feature *[Canberra the Great](/wiki/Canberra_the_Great "Canberra the Great")*.  

### Media {#Media}

As Australia's capital, Canberra is the most important centre for much of Australia's political reportage and thus all the major media, including the [Australian Broadcasting Corporation](/wiki/Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation "Australian Broadcasting Corporation"), the commercial television networks, and the metropolitan newspapers maintain local bureaus. News organisations are represented in the *[press gallery](/wiki/Canberra_Press_Gallery "Canberra Press Gallery")* , a group of journalists who report on the national [parliament](/wiki/Parliament_of_Australia "Parliament of Australia"). [The National Press Club of Australia](/wiki/National_Press_Club_of_Australia "National Press Club of Australia") in [Barton](/wiki/Barton,_Australian_Capital_Territory "Barton, Australian Capital Territory") has regular television broadcasts of its lunches at which a prominent guest, typically a politician or other public figure, delivers a speech followed by a question-and-answer session.^[\[294\]](#cite_note-299)^{#cite_ref-299}

Canberra has a daily newspaper, *[The Canberra Times](/wiki/The_Canberra_Times "The Canberra Times")* , which was established in 1926.^[\[295\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWigmore197187-300)^^[\[296\]](#cite_note-301)^ There are also several free weekly publications, including news magazines *CityNews* and *Canberra Weekly* as well as entertainment guide *[BMA Magazine](/wiki/BMA_Magazine "BMA Magazine")* . *BMA Magazine* first went to print in 1992; the inaugural edition featured coverage of the [Nirvana](/wiki/Nirvana_(band) "Nirvana (band)") [Nevermind](/wiki/Nevermind "Nevermind") tour.^[\[297\]](#cite_note-302)^{#cite_ref-302}

There are a number of AM and FM stations broadcasting in Canberra ([AM/FM Listing](/wiki/List_of_radio_station_callsigns_in_the_Australian_Capital_Territory "List of radio station callsigns in the Australian Capital Territory")). The main commercial operators are the [Capital Radio Network](/wiki/Capital_Radio_Network "Capital Radio Network") ([2CA](/wiki/2CA "2CA") and [2CC](/wiki/2CC "2CC")), and [Austereo](/wiki/Austereo "Austereo")/[ARN](/wiki/Australian_Radio_Network "Australian Radio Network") ([104.7](/wiki/104.7_(Canberra) "104.7 (Canberra)") and [Mix 106.3](/wiki/Mix_106.3 "Mix 106.3")). There are also several community operated stations.  

A DAB+ digital radio trial is also in operation, it simulcasts some of the AM/FM stations, and also provides several digital only stations ([DAB+ Trial Listing](/wiki/Digital_radio_in_Australia#Canberra "Digital radio in Australia")).

Five free-to-air television stations service Canberra:

* [ABC](/wiki/ABC_Television_(Australian_TV_network) "ABC Television (Australian TV network)") Canberra ([ABC](/wiki/ABC_Canberra_(TV_station) "ABC Canberra (TV station)"))
* [SBS](/wiki/Special_Broadcasting_Service "Special Broadcasting Service") New South Wales ([SBS](/wiki/SBS_(Australian_TV_channel) "SBS (Australian TV channel)"))
* [Network 10](/wiki/Network_10 "Network 10") Southern NSW \& ACT ([CTC](/wiki/CTC_(TV_station) "CTC (TV station)")) -- [Network 10](/wiki/Network_10 "Network 10") owned and operated station
* [Seven Network](/wiki/Seven_Network "Seven Network") Southern NSW \& ACT ([CBN](/wiki/CBN_(Australian_TV_station) "CBN (Australian TV station)")) -- [Seven Network](/wiki/Seven_Network "Seven Network") owned and operated station
* [WIN Television](/wiki/WIN_Television "WIN Television") Southern NSW \& ACT ([WIN](/wiki/WIN_(TV_station) "WIN (TV station)")) -- [Nine Network](/wiki/Nine_Network "Nine Network") affiliate

Each station broadcasts a primary channel and several [multichannels](/wiki/Digital_terrestrial_television_in_Australia#Additional_channels "Digital terrestrial television in Australia"). Of the three main commercial networks:

* WIN airs a half-hour local *[WIN News](/wiki/WIN_News "WIN News")* each weeknight at 6pm, produced from a newsroom in the city and broadcast from studios in [Wollongong](/wiki/Wollongong "Wollongong").
* Southern Cross 10 airs short local news updates throughout the day, produced and broadcast from its Hobart studios. It previously aired a regional edition of *[Nine News](/wiki/Nine_News "Nine News")* from Sydney each weeknight at 6pm, featuring opt-outs for Canberra and the ACT when it was a Nine affiliate.
* Seven airs short local news and weather updates throughout the day, produced and broadcast from its Canberra studios.

Prior to 1989, Canberra was serviced by just the ABC, SBS and Capital Television (CTC), which later became Ten Capital in 1994 then Southern Cross Ten in 2002 then Channel 9/Southern Cross Nine in 2016 and finally Channel 10 in 2021, with Prime Television (now Prime7) and WIN Television arriving as part of the Government's regional aggregation program in that year.^[\[298\]](#cite_note-303)^{#cite_ref-303}

[Pay television](/wiki/Pay_television "Pay television") services are available from [Foxtel](/wiki/Foxtel "Foxtel") (via satellite) and telecommunications company [TransACT](/wiki/TransACT "TransACT") (via cable).^[\[299\]](#cite_note-304)^{#cite_ref-304}  

### Sport {#Sport}

Main article: [Sport in the Australian Capital Territory](/wiki/Sport_in_the_Australian_Capital_Territory "Sport in the Australian Capital Territory")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/BruceStadium19032005.JPG/220px-BruceStadium19032005.JPG)](/wiki/File:BruceStadium19032005.JPG) A rugby league match at [Canberra Stadium](/wiki/Canberra_Stadium "Canberra Stadium")

In addition to local sporting leagues, Canberra has a number of sporting teams that compete in national and international competitions. The best known teams are the [Canberra Raiders](/wiki/Canberra_Raiders "Canberra Raiders") and the [ACT Brumbies](/wiki/ACT_Brumbies "ACT Brumbies") who play [rugby league](/wiki/Rugby_league "Rugby league") and [rugby union](/wiki/Rugby_union "Rugby union") respectively; both have been champions of their leagues.^[\[300\]](#cite_note-305)^^[\[301\]](#cite_note-306)^ Both teams play their home games at [Canberra Stadium](/wiki/Canberra_Stadium "Canberra Stadium"),^[\[302\]](#cite_note-307)^ which is the city's largest stadium and was used to hold group matches in [football](/wiki/Association_football "Association football") for the [2000 Summer Olympics](/wiki/2000_Summer_Olympics "2000 Summer Olympics") and in rugby union for the [2003 Rugby World Cup](/wiki/2003_Rugby_World_Cup "2003 Rugby World Cup").^[\[303\]](#cite_note-308)^^[\[304\]](#cite_note-309)^{#cite_ref-309}

[Canberra United](/wiki/Canberra_United_FC "Canberra United FC") represents the city in the [A-League Women](/wiki/A-League_Women "A-League Women") (formerly the W-League), the national [women's soccer](/wiki/Women%27s_association_football "Women's association football") league and were champions in the [2011--12 season](/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_W-League "2011–12 W-League").^[\[305\]](#cite_note-310)^ A men's team is set to join the [A-League Men](/wiki/A-League_Men "A-League Men") in the [2024--25 season](/wiki/2024%E2%80%9325_A-League_Men "2024–25 A-League Men").{#cite_ref-310}

The city also has a successful basketball team, the [Canberra Capitals](/wiki/Canberra_Capitals "Canberra Capitals"), which has won seven out of the last eleven [national women's basketball](/wiki/Women%27s_National_Basketball_League "Women's National Basketball League") titles.^[\[306\]](#cite_note-311)^ The [Canberra Vikings](/wiki/Canberra_Vikings "Canberra Vikings") represent the city in the [National Rugby Championship](/wiki/National_Rugby_Championship "National Rugby Championship") and finished second in the [2015 season](/wiki/2015_National_Rugby_Championship "2015 National Rugby Championship").{#cite_ref-311}

There are also teams that participate in national competitions in [netball](/wiki/Commonwealth_Bank_Trophy "Commonwealth Bank Trophy"), [field hockey](/wiki/Australian_Hockey_League "Australian Hockey League"), [ice hockey](/wiki/Australian_Ice_Hockey_League "Australian Ice Hockey League"), [cricket](/wiki/Futures_League "Futures League") and [baseball](/wiki/Australian_Baseball_League "Australian Baseball League").

The historic [Prime Minister's XI](/wiki/Prime_Minister%27s_XI "Prime Minister's XI") cricket match is played at [Manuka Oval](/wiki/Manuka_Oval "Manuka Oval") annually.^[\[307\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrowden2008200–210-312)^ Other significant annual sporting events include the [Canberra Marathon](/wiki/Canberra_Marathon "Canberra Marathon")^[\[308\]](#cite_note-Canberra_Marathon-313)^ and the City of Canberra Half Ironman Triathlon.{#cite_ref-Canberra_Marathon_313-0}

Canberra has been bidding for an [Australian Football League](/wiki/Australian_Football_League "Australian Football League") club since 1981 when [Australian rules in the Australian Capital Territory](/wiki/Australian_rules_football_in_the_Australian_Capital_Territory "Australian rules football in the Australian Capital Territory") was more popular.^[\[309\]](#cite_note-314)^ While the league has knocked back numerous proposals, according to the AFL Canberra belongs to the [Greater Western Sydney Giants](/wiki/Greater_Western_Sydney_Giants "Greater Western Sydney Giants")^[\[310\]](#cite_note-315)^ who play three home games at Manuka Oval each season.{#cite_ref-315}

Other significant annual sporting events include the [Canberra Marathon](/wiki/Canberra_Marathon "Canberra Marathon")^[\[308\]](#cite_note-Canberra_Marathon-313)^ and the City of Canberra Half Ironman Triathlon.{#cite_ref-Canberra_Marathon_313-1}

The [Australian Institute of Sport](/wiki/Australian_Institute_of_Sport "Australian Institute of Sport") (AIS) is located in the Canberra suburb of [Bruce](/wiki/Bruce,_Australian_Capital_Territory "Bruce, Australian Capital Territory").^[\[311\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTESparke1988304-316)^ The AIS is a specialised educational and training institution providing coaching for elite junior and senior athletes in a number of sports. The AIS has been operating since 1981 and has achieved significant success in producing elite athletes, both local and international.^[\[311\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTESparke1988304-316)^ The majority of Australia's team members and medallists at the [2000 Summer Olympics](/wiki/2000_Summer_Olympics "2000 Summer Olympics") in Sydney were AIS graduates.^[\[312\]](#cite_note-317)^{#cite_ref-317}

Canberra has numerous sporting ovals, golf courses, skate parks, and swimming pools that are open to the public. Tennis courts include those at the National Sports Club, [Lyneham](/wiki/Lyneham,_Australian_Capital_Territory "Lyneham, Australian Capital Territory"), former home of the [Canberra Women's Tennis Classic](/wiki/Canberra_Women%27s_Tennis_Classic "Canberra Women's Tennis Classic"). A Canberra-wide series of bicycle paths are available to cyclists for recreational and sporting purposes. Canberra Nature Parks have a large range of walking paths, horse and mountain bike trails. Water sports like sailing, rowing, dragon boating and water skiing are held on Canberra's lakes.^[\[313\]](#cite_note-318)^^[\[314\]](#cite_note-319)^ The [Rally of Canberra](/wiki/Rally_of_Canberra "Rally of Canberra") is an annual motor sport event, and from 2000 to 2002, Canberra hosted the [Canberra 400](/wiki/Canberra_400 "Canberra 400") event for [V8 Supercars](/wiki/V8_Supercars "V8 Supercars") on the temporary [Canberra Street Circuit](/wiki/Canberra_Street_Circuit "Canberra Street Circuit"), which was located inside the Parliamentary Triangle.{#cite_ref-319}

A popular form of exercise for people working near or in the Parliamentary Triangle is to do the "bridge to bridge walk/run" of about 5 km around [Lake Burley Griffin](/wiki/Lake_Burley_Griffin "Lake Burley Griffin"), crossing the [Commonwealth Avenue Bridge](/wiki/Commonwealth_Avenue_Bridge "Commonwealth Avenue Bridge") and [Kings Avenue Bridge](/wiki/Kings_Avenue,_Canberra "Kings Avenue, Canberra"), using the paths beside the lake. The walk takes about 1 hour, making it ideal for a lunchtime excursion. This is also popular on weekends. Such was the popularity during the [COVID-19](/wiki/COVID-19 "COVID-19") [isolation in 2020](/wiki/2020_coronavirus_pandemic_in_Australia#Australian_Capital_Territory "2020 coronavirus pandemic in Australia") that the ACT Government initiated a 'Clockwise is COVID-wise' rule for walkers and runners.^[\[315\]](#cite_note-2020-04-19_ABC-320)^{#cite_ref-2020-04-19_ABC_320-0}  

Infrastructure {#Infrastructure}
--------------------------------

### Health {#Health}

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Canberra_Hospital_February_2018.jpg/220px-Canberra_Hospital_February_2018.jpg)](/wiki/File:Canberra_Hospital_February_2018.jpg) The [Canberra Hospital](/wiki/Canberra_Hospital "Canberra Hospital")

Canberra has two large public hospitals, the approximately 600-bed [Canberra Hospital](/wiki/Canberra_Hospital "Canberra Hospital")---formerly the Woden Valley Hospital---in [Garran](/wiki/Garran,_Australian_Capital_Territory "Garran, Australian Capital Territory") and the 174-bed Calvary Public Hospital in [Bruce](/wiki/Bruce,_Australian_Capital_Territory "Bruce, Australian Capital Territory"). Both are teaching institutions.^[\[316\]](#cite_note-hos-321)^^[\[317\]](#cite_note-322)^^[\[318\]](#cite_note-calvary-act1-323)^^[\[319\]](#cite_note-324)^ The largest private hospital is the Calvary John James Hospital in [Deakin](/wiki/Deakin,_Australian_Capital_Territory "Deakin, Australian Capital Territory").^[\[320\]](#cite_note-325)^^[\[321\]](#cite_note-326)^ Calvary Private Hospital in Bruce and [Healthscope](/wiki/Healthscope "Healthscope")'s National Capital Private Hospital in Garran are also major healthcare providers.^[\[316\]](#cite_note-hos-321)^^[\[318\]](#cite_note-calvary-act1-323)^{#cite_ref-calvary-act1_323-1}

The [Royal Canberra Hospital](/wiki/Royal_Canberra_Hospital "Royal Canberra Hospital") was located on [Acton Peninsula](/wiki/Acton_Peninsula "Acton Peninsula") on [Lake Burley Griffin](/wiki/Lake_Burley_Griffin "Lake Burley Griffin"); it was closed in 1991 and was demolished in 1997 in a [controversial and fatal implosion](/wiki/Royal_Canberra_Hospital_implosion "Royal Canberra Hospital implosion") to facilitate construction of the [National Museum of Australia](/wiki/National_Museum_of_Australia "National Museum of Australia").^[\[113\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTENational_Capital_Development_Commission198818-113)^^[\[167\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTENational_Capital_Development_Commission198817-167)^^[\[174\]](#cite_note-map-174)^^[\[322\]](#cite_note-327)^^[\[323\]](#cite_note-328)^ The city has 10 aged care facilities. Canberra's hospitals receive emergency cases from throughout southern New South Wales,^[\[324\]](#cite_note-329)^ and [ACT Ambulance Service](/wiki/ACT_Ambulance_Service "ACT Ambulance Service") is one of four operational agencies of the [ACT Emergency Services Authority](/wiki/ACT_Emergency_Services_Authority "ACT Emergency Services Authority").^[\[325\]](#cite_note-330)^ [NETS](/wiki/Newborn_Emergency_Transport_Service "Newborn Emergency Transport Service") provides a dedicated ambulance service for inter-hospital transport of sick newborns within the ACT and into surrounding New South Wales.^[\[326\]](#cite_note-331)^{#cite_ref-331}  

### Transport {#Transport}

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Highways_into_Canberra_%286768361501%29.jpg/220px-Highways_into_Canberra_%286768361501%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Highways_into_Canberra_(6768361501).jpg) The [Glenloch Interchange](/wiki/Glenloch_Interchange "Glenloch Interchange") connects the [Tuggeranong Parkway](/wiki/Tuggeranong_Parkway "Tuggeranong Parkway") with [Parkes Way](/wiki/Parkes_Way "Parkes Way") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/ACTION_%28BUS_680%29_Volgren_Optimus_bodied_Scania_K360UA_6x2-2_%28Euro_VI%29_at_the_intersection_of_Alinga_St_and_Northbourne_Ave_%281%29.jpg/220px-ACTION_%28BUS_680%29_Volgren_Optimus_bodied_Scania_K360UA_6x2-2_%28Euro_VI%29_at_the_intersection_of_Alinga_St_and_Northbourne_Ave_%281%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:ACTION_(BUS_680)_Volgren_Optimus_bodied_Scania_K360UA_6x2-2_(Euro_VI)_at_the_intersection_of_Alinga_St_and_Northbourne_Ave_(1).jpg) [ACTION](/wiki/ACTION "ACTION") [Volgren](/wiki/Volgren "Volgren") bodied [Scania K360UA](/wiki/Scania_K-series "Scania K-series") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Tram_at_Alinga_Street_light_rail_stop_July_2022.jpg/220px-Tram_at_Alinga_Street_light_rail_stop_July_2022.jpg)](/wiki/File:Tram_at_Alinga_Street_light_rail_stop_July_2022.jpg) [Alinga Street light rail station](/wiki/Alinga_Street_light_rail_station "Alinga Street light rail station")

The automobile is by far the dominant form of transport in Canberra.^[\[327\]](#cite_note-road-332)^ The city is laid out so that arterial roads connecting inhabited clusters run through undeveloped areas of open land or forest, which results in a low population density;^[\[328\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPenguin_Books_Australia200023–25-333)^ this also means that idle land is available for the development of future transport corridors if necessary without the need to build tunnels or acquire developed residential land. In contrast, other capital cities in Australia have substantially less green space.^[\[329\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPenguin_Books_Australia20003–6,_32–35,_53–59,_74–77,_90–91,_101–104-334)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPenguin_Books_Australia20003–6,_32–35,_53–59,_74–77,_90–91,_101–104_334-0}

[Canberra's districts](/wiki/Suburbs_of_Canberra#Districts "Suburbs of Canberra") are generally connected by [parkways](/wiki/Parkway "Parkway")---limited access [dual carriageway](/wiki/Dual_carriageway "Dual carriageway") roads^[\[327\]](#cite_note-road-332)^^[\[330\]](#cite_note-335)^ with speed limits generally set at a maximum of 100 km/h (62 mph).^[\[331\]](#cite_note-336)^^[\[332\]](#cite_note-337)^ An example is the [Tuggeranong Parkway](/wiki/Tuggeranong_Parkway "Tuggeranong Parkway") which links Canberra's CBD and Tuggeranong, and bypasses Weston Creek.^[\[333\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUniversal_Publishers200757,_67,_77-338)^ In most districts, discrete residential suburbs are bounded by main arterial roads with only a few residential linking in, to deter non-local traffic from cutting through areas of housing.^[\[334\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUniversal_Publishers20071–100-339)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUniversal_Publishers20071–100_339-0}

In an effort to improve road safety, traffic cameras were first introduced to Canberra by the [Kate Carnell](/wiki/Kate_Carnell "Kate Carnell") Government in 1999.^[\[335\]](#cite_note-LawsonTraffic-340)^ The traffic cameras installed in Canberra include fixed red-light and speed cameras and point-to-point speed cameras; together they bring in revenue of approximately $11 million per year in fines.^[\[335\]](#cite_note-LawsonTraffic-340)^{#cite_ref-LawsonTraffic_340-1}

[ACTION](/wiki/ACTION "ACTION"), the government-operated bus service, provides public transport throughout the city.^[\[336\]](#cite_note-341)^ [CDC Canberra](/wiki/CDC_Canberra "CDC Canberra") provides bus services between Canberra and nearby areas of New South Wales of ([Murrumbateman](/wiki/Murrumbateman "Murrumbateman") and [Yass](/wiki/Yass,_New_South_Wales "Yass, New South Wales"))^[\[337\]](#cite_note-342)^ and as Qcity Transit ([Queanbeyan](/wiki/Queanbeyan "Queanbeyan")).^[\[338\]](#cite_note-343)^ A [light rail line](/wiki/Light_rail_in_Canberra "Light rail in Canberra") commenced service on 20 April 2019 linking the CBD with the northern district of [Gungahlin](/wiki/Gungahlin "Gungahlin").^[\[339\]](#cite_note-344)^ A planned Stage 2A of Canberra's light rail network will run from Alinga Street station to Commonwealth Park, adding three new stops at City West, City South and Commonwealth Park.^[\[340\]](#cite_note-345)^ In February 2021 ACT Minister for Transport and City Services Chris Steel said he expects construction on Stage 2A to commence in the 2021-22 financial year, and for "tracks to be laid" by the next Territory election in 2024.^[\[341\]](#cite_note-346)^ At the 2016 census, 7.1% of the journeys to work involved public transport, while 4.5% walked to work.^[\[241\]](#cite_note-Census2016-241)^{#cite_ref-Census2016_241-3}

There are two local taxi companies. [Aerial Capital Group](/wiki/Aerial_Consolidated_Transport "Aerial Consolidated Transport") enjoyed monopoly status until the arrival of Cabxpress in 2007.^[\[342\]](#cite_note-347)^ In October 2015 the ACT Government passed legislation to regulate ride sharing, allowing ride share services including [Uber](/wiki/Uber "Uber") to operate legally in Canberra.^[\[343\]](#cite_note-348)^^[\[344\]](#cite_note-349)^^[\[345\]](#cite_note-350)^ The ACT Government was the first jurisdiction in Australia to enact legislation to regulate the service.^[\[346\]](#cite_note-351)^ Since then many other ride sharing and taxi services have started in ACT namely [Ola](/wiki/Ola_Cabs "Ola Cabs"), Glide Taxi^[\[347\]](#cite_note-352)^ and GoCatch^[\[348\]](#cite_note-353)^{#cite_ref-353}

An interstate [NSW TrainLink](/wiki/NSW_TrainLink "NSW TrainLink") railway service connects Canberra to Sydney.^[\[349\]](#cite_note-traindestinations-354)^ [Canberra railway station](/wiki/Canberra_railway_station "Canberra railway station") is in the inner south suburb of [Kingston](/wiki/Kingston,_Australian_Capital_Territory "Kingston, Australian Capital Territory").^[\[350\]](#cite_note-355)^ Between 1920 and 1922 the train line crossed the Molonglo River and ran as far north as the city centre, although the line was closed following major flooding and was never rebuilt, while plans for a line to [Yass](/wiki/Yass,_New_South_Wales "Yass, New South Wales") were abandoned. A [3 ft 6 in](/wiki/3_ft_6_in_gauge_railways "3 ft 6 in gauge railways") (1,067 mm) gauge construction railway was built in 1923 between the [Yarralumla brickworks](/wiki/Yarralumla_brickworks "Yarralumla brickworks") and the provisional Parliament House; it was later extended to Civic, but the whole line was closed in May 1927.^[\[351\]](#cite_note-356)^ Train services to Melbourne are provided by way of a NSW TrainLink bus service which connects with a rail service between Sydney and Melbourne in Yass, about a one-hour drive from Canberra.^[\[349\]](#cite_note-traindestinations-354)^^[\[352\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPenguin_Books_Australia200020-357)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPenguin_Books_Australia200020_357-0}

Plans to establish a [high-speed rail](/wiki/High-speed_rail_in_Australia "High-speed rail in Australia") service between Melbourne, Canberra and Sydney,^[\[353\]](#cite_note-358)^ have not been implemented, as the various proposals have been deemed economically unviable.^[\[354\]](#cite_note-359)^^[\[355\]](#cite_note-360)^ The original plans for Canberra included proposals for railed transport within the city,^[\[356\]](#cite_note-railways-361)^ however none eventuated.^[\[356\]](#cite_note-railways-361)^ The phase 2 report of the most recent proposal, the [High Speed Rail Study](/wiki/High-speed_rail_in_Australia#High-Speed_Rail_Study_(2008–2013) "High-speed rail in Australia"), was published by the [Department of Infrastructure and Transport](/wiki/Department_of_Infrastructure_and_Transport "Department of Infrastructure and Transport") on 11 April 2013.^[\[357\]](#cite_note-362)^ A railway connecting Canberra to [Jervis Bay](/wiki/Jervis_Bay "Jervis Bay") was also planned but never constructed.^[\[358\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGibbney198858,_60-363)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGibbney198858,_60_363-0}

Canberra is about three hours by road from Sydney on the [Federal Highway](/wiki/Federal_Highway_(Australia) "Federal Highway (Australia)") (National Highway 23),^[\[359\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPenguin_Books_Australia2000inside_cover-364)^ which connects with the [Hume Highway](/wiki/Hume_Highway "Hume Highway") (National Highway 31) near [Goulburn](/wiki/Goulburn "Goulburn"), and seven hours by road from Melbourne on the [Barton Highway](/wiki/Barton_Highway "Barton Highway") (National Highway 25), which joins the Hume Highway at Yass.^[\[359\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPenguin_Books_Australia2000inside_cover-364)^ It is a two-hour drive on the [Monaro Highway](/wiki/Monaro_Highway "Monaro Highway") (National Highway 23) to the ski fields of the [Snowy Mountains](/wiki/Snowy_Mountains "Snowy Mountains") and the [Kosciuszko National Park](/wiki/Kosciuszko_National_Park "Kosciuszko National Park").^[\[352\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPenguin_Books_Australia200020-357)^ [Batemans Bay](/wiki/Batemans_Bay "Batemans Bay"), a popular holiday spot on the New South Wales coast, is also two hours away via the [Kings Highway](/wiki/Kings_Highway,_Australia "Kings Highway, Australia").^[\[352\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPenguin_Books_Australia200020-357)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPenguin_Books_Australia200020_357-2}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Canberra_International_Airport_01.jpg/220px-Canberra_International_Airport_01.jpg)](/wiki/File:Canberra_International_Airport_01.jpg) [Canberra Airport](/wiki/Canberra_Airport "Canberra Airport") terminal

[Canberra Airport](/wiki/Canberra_Airport "Canberra Airport") provides direct domestic services to [Adelaide](/wiki/Adelaide_Airport "Adelaide Airport"), [Brisbane](/wiki/Brisbane_Airport "Brisbane Airport"), [Cairns](/wiki/Cairns_Airport "Cairns Airport"), [Darwin](/wiki/Darwin_Airport "Darwin Airport"), [Gold Coast](/wiki/Gold_Coast_Airport "Gold Coast Airport"), [Hobart](/wiki/Hobart_Airport "Hobart Airport"), [Melbourne](/wiki/Melbourne_Airport "Melbourne Airport"), [Perth](/wiki/Perth_Airport "Perth Airport"), [Sunshine Coast](/wiki/Sunshine_Coast_Airport "Sunshine Coast Airport") and [Sydney](/wiki/Sydney_Airport "Sydney Airport") with connections to other domestic centres.^[\[360\]](#cite_note-365)^ There are also direct flights to small regional towns: [Ballina](/wiki/Ballina_Byron_Gateway_Airport "Ballina Byron Gateway Airport"), [Dubbo](/wiki/Dubbo_City_Airport "Dubbo City Airport"), [Newcastle](/wiki/Newcastle_Airport,_New_South_Wales "Newcastle Airport, New South Wales") and [Port Macquarie](/wiki/Port_Macquarie_Airport "Port Macquarie Airport") in New South Wales. Canberra Airport is, as of September 2013, designated by the [Australian Government Department of Infrastructure and Regional Development](/wiki/Department_of_Infrastructure_and_Regional_Development "Department of Infrastructure and Regional Development") as a restricted use designated international airport.^[\[361\]](#cite_note-366)^ International flights have previously been operated by both [Singapore Airlines](/wiki/Singapore_Airlines "Singapore Airlines") and [Qatar Airways](/wiki/Qatar_Airways "Qatar Airways"). [Fiji Airways](/wiki/Fiji_Airways "Fiji Airways") has announced direct flights to [Nadi](/wiki/Nadi "Nadi") commencing in July 2023.^[\[362\]](#cite_note-367)^ Until 2003 the civilian airport shared runways with [RAAF Base Fairbairn](/wiki/Fairbairn_airbase "Fairbairn airbase"). In June of that year, the Air Force base was decommissioned and from that time the airport was fully under civilian control.^[\[363\]](#cite_note-368)^{#cite_ref-368}

Canberra has one of the highest rates of active travel of all Australian major cities, with 7.1 per cent of commuters walking or cycling to work in 2011.^[\[364\]](#cite_note-369)^ An ACT Government survey conducted in late 2010 found that Canberrans walk an average of 26 minutes each day.^[\[365\]](#cite_note-370)^ According to *The Canberra Times* in March 2014, Canberra's cyclists are involved in an average of four reported collisions every week.^[\[366\]](#cite_note-371)^ The newspaper also reported that Canberra is home to 87,000 cyclists, translating to the highest cycling participation rate in Australia; and, with higher popularity, bike injury rates in 2012 were twice the national average.^[\[367\]](#cite_note-372)^{#cite_ref-372}

Since late 2020, two [scooter-sharing systems](/wiki/Scooter-sharing_system "Scooter-sharing system") have been operational in Canberra: orange scooters from Neuron Mobility and purple scooters from Beam Mobility,^[\[368\]](#cite_note-373)^ both [Singapore](/wiki/Singapore "Singapore")-based companies that operate in many Australian cities. These services cover much of [Canberra Central](/wiki/Canberra_Central "Canberra Central") and Central [Belconnen](/wiki/Belconnen "Belconnen"), with plans to expand coverage to more areas of the city in 2022.^[\[369\]](#cite_note-374)^{#cite_ref-374}  

### Utilities {#Utilities}

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Mount_Majura_Solar_Farm_August_2024.jpg/220px-Mount_Majura_Solar_Farm_August_2024.jpg)](/wiki/File:Mount_Majura_Solar_Farm_August_2024.jpg) The [Mount Majura Solar Farm](/wiki/Mount_Majura_Solar_Farm "Mount Majura Solar Farm") has a rated output of 2.3 megawatts and was opened on 6 October 2016.^[\[370\]](#cite_note-Solar_Choice-375)^

The government-owned [Icon Water](/wiki/Icon_Water "Icon Water") manages Canberra's water and sewerage infrastructure.^[\[371\]](#cite_note-376)^ [ActewAGL](/wiki/ActewAGL "ActewAGL") is a joint venture between ACTEW and [AGL](/wiki/Australian_Gas_Light_Company "Australian Gas Light Company"), and is the retail provider of Canberra's utility services including water, natural gas, electricity, and also some telecommunications services via a subsidiary [TransACT](/wiki/TransACT "TransACT").^[\[372\]](#cite_note-377)^{#cite_ref-377}

Canberra's water is stored in four reservoirs, the Corin, Bendora and Cotter dams on the [Cotter River](/wiki/Cotter_River "Cotter River") and the Googong Dam on the Queanbeyan River. Although the Googong Dam is located in New South Wales, it is managed by the ACT government.^[\[373\]](#cite_note-378)^ Icon Water owns Canberra's two wastewater treatment plants, located at [Fyshwick](/wiki/Fyshwick "Fyshwick") and on the lower reaches of the [Molonglo River](/wiki/Molonglo_River "Molonglo River").^[\[374\]](#cite_note-379)^^[\[375\]](#cite_note-380)^{#cite_ref-380}

[Electricity for Canberra](/wiki/Energy_in_the_Australian_Capital_Territory "Energy in the Australian Capital Territory") mainly comes from the national power grid through substations at [Holt](/wiki/Holt,_Australian_Capital_Territory "Holt, Australian Capital Territory") and [Fyshwick](/wiki/Fyshwick "Fyshwick") (via [Queanbeyan](/wiki/Queanbeyan "Queanbeyan")).^[\[376\]](#cite_note-381)^ Power was first supplied from the [Kingston Powerhouse](/wiki/Kingston_Powerhouse "Kingston Powerhouse") near the Molonglo River, a thermal plant built in 1913, but this was finally closed in 1957.^[\[377\]](#cite_note-382)^^[\[378\]](#cite_note-383)^ The ACT has four solar farms, which were opened between 2014 and 2017: [Royalla](/wiki/Royalla_Solar_Farm "Royalla Solar Farm") (rated output of 20 megawatts, 2014),^[\[379\]](#cite_note-384)^ [Mount Majura](/wiki/Mount_Majura_Solar_Farm "Mount Majura Solar Farm") (2.3 MW, 2016),^[\[370\]](#cite_note-Solar_Choice-375)^ [Mugga Lane](/wiki/Mugga_Lane_Solar_Park "Mugga Lane Solar Park") (13 MW, 2017)^[\[380\]](#cite_note-385)^ and [Williamsdale](/wiki/Williamsdale_Solar_Farm "Williamsdale Solar Farm") (11 MW, 2017).^[\[381\]](#cite_note-386)^ In addition, numerous houses in Canberra have photovoltaic panels or solar hot water systems. In 2015 and 2016, rooftop solar systems supported by the ACT government's feed-in tariff had a capacity of 26.3 megawatts, producing 34,910 MWh. In the same year, retailer-supported schemes had a capacity of 25.2 megawatts and exported 28,815 MWh to the grid (power consumed locally was not recorded).^[\[382\]](#cite_note-387)^{#cite_ref-387}

There are no wind-power generators in Canberra, but several have been built or are being built or planned in nearby New South Wales, such as the 140.7 megawatt [Capital Wind Farm](/wiki/Capital_Wind_Farm "Capital Wind Farm"). The ACT government announced in 2013 that it was raising the target for electricity consumed in the ACT to be supplied from renewable sources to 90% by 2020,^[\[186\]](#cite_note-renewable-186)^ raising the target from 210 to 550 megawatts.^[\[383\]](#cite_note-388)^ It announced in February 2015 that three wind farms in Victoria and South Australia would supply 200 megawatts of capacity; these are expected to be operational by 2017.^[\[384\]](#cite_note-389)^ Contracts for the purchase of an additional 200 megawatts of power from two wind farms in South Australia and New South Wales were announced in December 2015 and March 2016.^[\[385\]](#cite_note-390)^^[\[386\]](#cite_note-391)^ The ACT government announced in 2014 that up to 23 megawatts of feed-in-tariff entitlements would be made available for the establishment of a facility in the ACT or surrounding region for burning household and business waste to produce electricity by 2020.^[\[387\]](#cite_note-392)^{#cite_ref-392}

The ACT has the highest rate with internet access at home (94 per cent of households in 2014--15).^[\[388\]](#cite_note-393)^{#cite_ref-393}  

Twin towns and sister cities {#Twin_towns_and_sister_cities}
------------------------------------------------------------

See also: [List of twin towns and sister cities in Oceania](/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Oceania "List of twin towns and sister cities in Oceania")

Canberra has three [sister cities](/wiki/Sister_city "Sister city"):

* [Beijing](/wiki/Beijing "Beijing"), China^[\[291\]](#cite_note-Canberra-296)^{#cite_ref-Canberra_296-1}
* [Nara](/wiki/Nara,_Nara "Nara, Nara"), Japan^[\[291\]](#cite_note-Canberra-296)^{#cite_ref-Canberra_296-2}
* [Wellington](/wiki/Wellington "Wellington"), New Zealand^[\[389\]](#cite_note-394)^{#cite_ref-394}

In addition, Canberra has the following friendship cities:

* [Hangzhou](/wiki/Hangzhou "Hangzhou"), China: The ACT Government signed a Memorandum of Understanding with the Hangzhou Municipal People's Government on 29 October 1998. The Agreement was designed to promote business opportunities and cultural exchanges between the two cities.^[\[390\]](#cite_note-395)^{#cite_ref-395}
* [Dili](/wiki/Dili "Dili"), East Timor: The Canberra Dili Friendship Agreement was signed in 2004, aiming to build friendship and mutual respect and promote educational, cultural, economic, humanitarian and sporting links between Canberra and Dili.^[\[391\]](#cite_note-396)^{#cite_ref-396}
